\"sort\"}\n   588→\t\tfor _, prop := range legacyTableProps {\n   589→\t\t\tif _, exists := panel[prop]; exists {\n   590→\t\t\t\tif autoMigrateFrom, hasAutoMigrate := panel[\"autoMigrateFrom\"]; hasAutoMigrate && autoMigrateFrom == \"table-old\" {\n   591→\t\t\t\t\tif !originalProperties[prop] {\n   592→\t\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n   593→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   594→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   595→\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n   596→\t\t\t\t}\n   597→\t\t\t}\n   598→\t\t}\n   599→\t}\n   600→\n   601→\t// Remove properties that match defaults, but preserve properties that were originally present\n   602→\tfor prop, defaultValue := range defaults {\n   603→\t\tif panelValue, exists := panel[prop]; exists {\n   604→\t\t\tif isEqual(panelValue, defaultValue) {\n   605→\t\t\t\t// Special case: fieldConfig - handle preservation of original custom object first\n   606→\t\t\t\tif prop == \"fieldConfig\" {\n   607→\t\t\t\t\t// Check if we need to preserve the custom object before removing fieldConfig\n   608→\t\t\t\t\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n   609→\t\t\t\t\t\t// Ensure fieldConfig structure exists with custom object\n   610→\t\t\t\t\t\tif fieldConfig, ok := panelValue.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   611→\t\t\t\t\t\t\tif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   612→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tif _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n   613→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tdefaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n   614→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   615→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\t// Don't remove fieldConfig if we added custom back\n   616→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   617→\t\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   618→\t\t\t\t\t\t}\n   619→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   620→\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n   621→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   622→\t\t\t\t\t// Only remove if it wasn't originally present in the input\n   623→\t\t\t\t\tif !originalProperties[prop] {\n   624→\t\t\t\t\t\tdelete(panel, prop)\n   625→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   626→\t\t\t\t}\n   627→\t\t\t}\n   628→\t\t}\n   629→\t}\n   630→\n   631→\t// Remove empty targets arrays (frontend removes them in cleanup)\n   632→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(panel, \"targets\", []interface{}{})\n   633→\n   634→\t// Handle case where fieldConfig was removed but originally had custom object\n   635→\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n   636→\t\tif _, hasFieldConfig := panel[\"fieldConfig\"]; !hasFieldConfig {\n   637→\t\t\t// Recreate fieldConfig with custom object\n   638→\t\t\tpanel[\"fieldConfig\"] = map[string]interface{}{\n   639→\t\t\t\t\"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n   640→\t\t\t\t\t\"custom\": map[string]interface{}{},\n   641→\t\t\t\t},\n   642→\t\t\t\t\"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n   643→\t\t\t}\n   644→\t\t}\n   645→\t}\n   646→\n   647→\t// Clean up fieldConfig to match frontend behavior\n   648→\tif fieldConfig, exists := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{}); exists {\n   649→\t\t// Clean up fieldConfig defaults to match frontend behavior\n   650→\t\tif defaults, hasDefaults := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); hasDefaults {\n   651→\t\t\t// Remove properties that frontend considers as defaults and omits\n   652→\t\t\tcleanupFieldConfigDefaults(defaults, panel)\n   653→\n   654→\t\t\t// Preserve custom object if it was originally present, even if empty\n   655→\t\t\tif panel[\"_originallyHadFieldConfigCustom\"] == true {\n   656→\t\t\t\tif _, hasCustom := defaults[\"custom\"]; !hasCustom {\n   657→\t\t\t\t\tdefaults[\"custom\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n   658→\t\t\t\t}\n   659→\t\t\t}\n   660→\t\t}\n   661→\t}\n   662→}\n   663→\n   664→// isEqual checks if two values are equal (simplified version)\n   665→func isEqual(a, b interface{}) bool {\n   666→\tif a == nil && b == nil {\n   667→\t\treturn true\n   668→\t}\n   669→\tif a == nil || b == nil {\n   670→\t\treturn false\n   671→\t}\n   672→\n   673→\t// For simple types, use direct comparison\n   674→\tswitch aVal := a.(type) {\n   675→\tcase bool:\n   676→\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(bool); ok {\n   677→\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   678→\t\t}\n   679→\tcase string:\n   680→\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(string); ok {\n   681→\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   682→\t\t}\n   683→\tcase float64:\n   684→\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(float64); ok {\n   685→\t\t\treturn aVal == bVal\n   686→\t\t}\n   687→\tcase []interface{}:\n   688→\t\tif bVal, ok := b.([]interface{}); ok {\n   689→\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n   690→\t\t\t\treturn false\n   691→\t\t\t}\n   692→\t\t\tfor i, v := range aVal {\n   693→\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[i]) {\n   694→\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n   695→\t\t\t\t}\n   696→\t\t\t}\n   697→\t\t\treturn true\n   698→\t\t}\n   699→\tcase map[string]interface{}:\n   700→\t\tif bVal, ok := b.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   701→\t\t\tif len(aVal) != len(bVal) {\n   702→\t\t\t\treturn false\n   703→\t\t\t}\n   704→\t\t\tfor k, v := range aVal {\n   705→\t\t\t\tif !isEqual(v, bVal[k]) {\n   706→\t\t\t\t\treturn false\n   707→\t\t\t\t}\n   708→\t\t\t}\n   709→\t\t\treturn true\n   710→\t\t}\n   711→\t}\n   712→\n   713→\treturn false\n   714→}\n   715→\n   716→// cleanupDashboardForSave applies the same cleanup logic as the frontend\n   717→func cleanupDashboardForSave(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n   718→\tremoveNonPersistedProperties(dashboard)\n   719→\tremoveNullValues(dashboard)\n   720→\tcleanupTemplating(dashboard)\n   721→\tcleanupPanels(dashboard)\n   722→\tcleanupDashboardDefaults(dashboard)\n   723→}\n   724→\n   725→// removeNonPersistedProperties removes non-persisted dashboard properties\n   726→func removeNonPersistedProperties(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n   727→\tnonPersistedProperties := map[string]bool{\n   728→\t\t\"events\":                           true,\n   729→\t\t\"meta\":                             true,\n   730→\t\t\"panels\":                           true, // handled specially below\n   731→\t\t\"templating\":                       true, // handled specially below\n   732→\t\t\"originalTime\":                     true,\n   733→\t\t\"originalTemplating\":               true,\n   734→\t\t\"originalLibraryPanels\":            true,\n   735→\t\t\"panelInEdit\":                      true,\n   736→\t\t\"panelInView\":                      true,\n   737→\t\t\"getVariablesFromState\":            true,\n   738→\t\t\"formatDate\":                       true,\n   739→\t\t\"appEventsSubscription\":            true,\n   740→\t\t\"panelsAffectedByVariableChange\":   true,\n   741→\t\t\"lastRefresh\":                      true,\n   742→\t\t\"timeRangeUpdatedDuringEditOrView\": true,\n   743→\t\t\"originalDashboard\":                true,\n   744→\t}\n   745→\n   746→\tfor k, v := range nonPersistedProperties {\n   747→\t\t// Do not remove \"panels\" and \"templating\" here, as they are handled specially\n   748→\t\tif (k == \"panels\" || k == \"templating\") && v {\n   749→\t\t\tcontinue\n   750→\t\t}\n   751→\t\tif v {\n   752→\t\t\tdelete(dashboard, k)\n   753→\t\t}\n   754→\t}\n   755→\n   756→\t// Remove properties that frontend omits in getSaveModel\n   757→\tdelete(dashboard, \"variables\")\n   758→}\n   759→\n   760→// removeNullValues removes null values to match frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior\n   761→func removeNullValues(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n   762→\t// This handles gnetId: null and other null properties\n   763→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"gnetId\", nil)\n   764→}\n   765→\n   766→// cleanupTemplating cleans up templating to match frontend's getTemplatingSaveModel 769→\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursively(templating)\n   770→\t\tcleanupTemplatingVariables(templating)\n   771→\t}\n   772→}\n   773→\n   774→// cleanupTemplatingVariables applies variable adapter logic\n   775→func cleanupTemplatingVariables(templating map[string]interface{}) {\n   776→\tif list, ok := templating[\"list\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n   777→\t\tfor _, variableInterface := range list {\n   778→\t\t\tif variable, ok := variableInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   779→\t\t\t\tcleanupVariable(variable)\n   780→\t\t\t}\n   781→\t\t}\n   782→\t}\n   783→}\n   784→\n   785→// cleanupVariable cleans up individual variable properties\n   786→func cleanupVariable(variable map[string]interface{}) {\n   787→\t// Remove null datasource\n   788→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(variable, \"datasource\", nil)\n   789→\n   790→\t// Remove properties that frontend omits in getSaveModel\n   791→\tdelete(variable, \"index\")\n   792→\n   793→\t// Apply variable type-specific logic\n   794→\tif variableType, ok := variable[\"type\"].(string); ok {\n   795→\t\tswitch variableType {\n   796→\t\tcase \"query\":\n   797→\t\t\t// Query variables: keep options: [] if refresh !== never (matches frontend getSaveModel logic)\n   798→\t\t\trefresh := schemaversion.GetIntValue(variable, \"refresh\", 1) // Default to 1 (onDashboardLoad) if not specified\n   799→\t\t\tif refresh != 0 {                                            // 0 = VariableRefreshNever\n   800→\t\t\t\tif _, hasOptions := variable[\"options\"]; !hasOptions {\n   801→\t\t\t\t\tvariable[\"options\"] = []interface{}{}\n   802→\t\t\t\t}\n   803→\t\t\t}\n   804→\t\tcase \"constant\":\n   805→\t\t\t// Constant variables: remove options completely\n   806→\t\t\tdelete(variable, \"options\")\n   807→\t\tcase \"datasource\":\n   808→\t\t\t// Datasource variables: always set options to empty array\n   809→\t\t\tvariable[\"options\"] = []interface{}{}\n   810→\t\tcase \"custom\":\n   811→\t\t\t// Custom variables: no special handling (just return rest)\n   812→\t\t\t// This is the default behavior - no additional processing needed\n   813→\t\tcase \"textbox\":\n   814→\t\t\t// Textbox variables: handle query vs originalQuery logic\n   815→\t\t\t// For now, just return rest (no special handling needed for basic cases)\n   816→\t\tcase \"adhoc\":\n   817→\t\t\t// Adhoc variables: no special handling\n   818→\t\t\t// This is the default behavior - no additional processing needed\n   819→\t\t}\n   820→\t}\n   821→}\n   822→\n   823→// cleanupPanels cleans up panels and ensures panels property always exists\n   824→func cleanupPanels(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n   825→\tif panels, ok := dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n   826→\t\t// Filter out repeated panels (matches frontend getPanelSaveModels behavior)\n   827→\t\t// Frontend filters: !(panel.repeatPanelId || panel.repeatedByRow)\n   828→\t\tfilteredPanels := []interface{}{}\n   829→\t\tfor _, panelInterface := range panels {\n   830→\t\t\tif panel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   831→\t\t\t\t// Skip panels with repeatPanelId or repeatedByRow\n   832→\t\t\t\tif _, hasRepeatPanelId := panel[\"repeatPanelId\"]; hasRepeatPanelId {\n   833→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   834→\t\t\t\t}\n   835→\t\t\t\tif _, hasRepeatedByRow := panel[\"repeatedByRow\"]; hasRepeatedByRow {\n   836→\t\t\t\t\tcontinue\n   837→\t\t\t\t}\n   838→\t\t\t\tfilteredPanels = append(filteredPanels, panel)\n   839→\t\t\t}\n   840→\t\t}\n   841→\n   842→\t\tcleanupPanelList(filteredPanels)\n   843→\t\tsortPanelsByGridPosition(filteredPanels)\n   844→\t\tdashboard[\"panels\"] = filteredPanels\n   845→\t} else {\n   846→\t\t// Ensure panels property exists even if empty (matches frontend behavior)\n   847→\t\tdashboard[\"panels\"] = []interface{}{}\n   848→\t}\n   849→}\n   850→\n   851→// cleanupPanelList cleans up all panels including nested ones\n   852→func cleanupPanelList(panels []interface{}) {\n   853→\tfor _, panelInterface := range panels {\n   854→\t\tif panel, ok := panelInterface.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   855→\t\t\tcleanupPanelForSaveWithContext(panel, false)\n   856→\n   857→\t\t\t// Handle nested panels in row panels\n   858→\t\t\tif nestedPanels, ok := panel[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n   859→\t\t\t\tfor _, nestedPanelInterface := range 863→\t\t\t\t}\n   864→\t\t\t}\n   865→\t\t}\n   866→\t}\n   867→}\n   868→\n   869→// sortPanelsByGridPosition sorts panels by grid position (matches frontend sortPanelsByGridPos behavior)\n   870→func sortPanelsByGridPosition(panels []interface{}) {\n   871→\tsort.SliceStable(panels, func(i, j int) bool {\n   872→\t\tpanelA, okA := panels[i].(map[string]interface{})\n   873→\t\tpanelB, okB := panels[j].(map[string]interface{})\n   874→\t\tif !okA || !okB {\n   875→\t\t\treturn false\n   876→\t\t}\n   877→\n   878→\t\t// Get gridPos or use default values if missing\n   879→\t\tgridPosA, okA := panelA[\"gridPos\"].(map[string]interface{})\n   880→\t\tgridPosB, okB := panelB[\"gridPos\"].(map[string]interface{})\n   881→\n   882→\t\t// Default gridPos values (matches frontend PanelModel defaults)\n   883→\t\tdefaultY := float64(0)\n   884→\t\tdefaultX := float64(0)\n   885→\n   886→\t\tyA := defaultY\n   887→\t\tif okA {\n   888→\t\t\tif y, ok := gridPosA[\"y\"].(float64); ok {\n   889→\t\t\t\tyA = y\n   890→\t\t\t} else if y, ok := gridPosA[\"y\"].(int); ok {\n   891→\t\t\t\tyA = float64(y)\n   892→\t\t\t}\n   893→\t\t}\n   894→\n   895→\t\tyB := defaultY\n   896→\t\tif okB {\n   897→\t\t\tif y, ok := gridPosB[\"y\"].(float64); ok {\n   898→\t\t\t\tyB = y\n   899→\t\t\t} else if y, ok := gridPosB[\"y\"].(int); ok {\n   900→\t\t\t\tyB = float64(y)\n   901→\t\t\t}\n   902→\t\t}\n   903→\n   904→\t\tif yA == yB {\n   905→\t\t\txA := defaultX\n   906→\t\t\tif okA {\n   907→\t\t\t\tif x, ok := gridPosA[\"x\"].(float64); ok {\n   908→\t\t\t\t\txA = x\n   909→\t\t\t\t} else if x, ok := gridPosA[\"x\"].(int); ok {\n   910→\t\t\t\t\txA = float64(x)\n   911→\t\t\t\t}\n   912→\t\t\t}\n   913→\n   914→\t\t\txB := defaultX\n   915→\t\t\tif okB {\n   916→\t\t\t\tif x, ok := gridPosB[\"x\"].(float64); ok {\n   917→\t\t\t\t\txB = x\n   918→\t\t\t\t} else if x, ok := gridPosB[\"x\"].(int); ok {\n   919→\t\t\t\t\txB = float64(x)\n   920→\t\t\t\t}\n   921→\t\t\t}\n   922→\t\t\treturn xA < xB\n   923→\t\t}\n   924→\t\treturn yA < yB\n   925→\t})\n   926→}\n   927→\n   928→// cleanupRowPanelProperties removes default row panel properties that frontend filters out\n   929→func cleanupRowPanelProperties(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n   930→\tpanelType, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string)\n   931→\tif !ok || panelType != \"row\" {\n   932→\t\treturn\n   933→\t}\n   934→\n   935→\t// Remove repeat if empty string (default value)\n   936→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(panel, \"repeat\", \"\")\n   937→}\n   938→\n   939→// applyPanelAutoMigration applies the same auto-migration logic as the frontend PanelModel constructor\n   940→func applyPanelAutoMigration(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n   941→\tpanelType, ok := panel[\"type\"].(string)\n   942→\tif !ok {\n   943→\t\treturn\n   944→\t}\n   945→\n   946→\tvar newType string\n   947→\n   948→\t// Graph needs special logic as it can be migrated to multiple panels\n   949→\t// Including graphite which was previously migrated to graph in the schema version 2 migration in DashboardMigrator.ts\n   950→\t// but this was a bug because in there graphite was set to graph, but since those migrations run\n   951→\t// after PanelModel.restoreModel where autoMigrateFrom is set, this caused the graph migration to be skipped.\n   952→\t// And this resulted in a dashboard with invalid panels.\n   953→\tif panelType == \"graph\" || panelType == \"graphite\" {\n   954→\t\t// Check xaxis mode for special cases\n   955→\t\tnewType = getGraphAutoMigration(panel)\n   956→\t} else {\n   957→\t\t// Check autoMigrateAngular mapping\n   958→\t\tautoMigrateAngular := map[string]string{\n   959→\t\t\t\"table-old\":                \"table\",\n   960→\t\t\t\"singlestat\":               \"stat\",\n   961→\t\t\t\"grafana-singlestat-panel\": \"stat\",\n   962→\t\t\t\"grafana-piechart-panel\":   \"piechart\",\n   963→\t\t\t\"grafana-worldmap-panel\":   \"geomap\",\n   964→\t\t\t\"natel-discrete-panel\":     \"state-timeline\",\n   965→\t\t}\n   966→\n   967→\t\tif mappedType, exists := autoMigrateAngular[panelType]; exists {\n   968→\t\t\tnewType = mappedType\n   969→\t\t}\n   970→\t}\n   971→\n   972→\t// Apply auto-migration if a new type was determined\n   973→\tif newType != \"\" {\n   974→\t\tpanel[\"autoMigrateFrom\"] = panelType\n   975→\t\tpanel[\"type\"] = newType\n   976→\t}\n   977→}\n   978→\n   979→func getGraphAutoMigration(panel map[string]interface{}) string {\n   980→\tnewType := \"\"\n   981→\tif xaxis, ok := panel[\"xaxis\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   982→\t\tif mode, ok := xaxis[\"mode\"].(string); ok {\n   983→\t\t\tswitch mode {\n   984→\t\t\tcase \"series\":\n   985→\t\t\t\t// Check legend values for bargauge\n   986→\t\t\t\tif legend, ok := panel[\"legend\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n   987→\t\t\t\t\tif values, ok := legend[\"values\"].(bool); ok && values {\n   988→\t\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"bargauge\"\n   989→\t\t\t\t\t} else {\n   990→\t\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"barchart\"\n   991→\t\t\t\t\t}\n   992→\t\t\t\t} else {\n   993→\t\t\t\t\tnewType = \"barchart\"\n   994→\t\t\t\t}\n   995→\t\t\tcase \"histogram\":\n   996→\t\t\t\tnewType = \"histogram\"\n   997→\t\t\t}\n   998→\t\t}\n   999→\t}\n  1000→\n  1001→\t// Default graph migration to timeseries\n  1002→\tif newType == \"\" {\n  1003→\t\tnewType = \"timeseries\"\n  1004→\t}\n  1005→\n  1006→\treturn newType\n  1007→}\n  1008→\n  1009→// removeNullValuesRecursively removes null values from nested objects and arrays\n  1010→// This matches the frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior\n  1011→func removeNullValuesRecursively(data interface{}) {\n  1012→\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(data, \"\")\n  1013→}\n  1014→\n  1015→// removeNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext removes null values from nested objects and arrays\n  1016→// This matches the frontend's JSON.stringify/parse behavior in getSaveModelClone()\n  1017→func removeNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(data interface{}, panelType string) {\n  1018→\tswitch v := data.(type) {\n  1019→\tcase map[string]interface{}:\n  1020→\t\t// Remove null values from map\n  1021→\t\tfor key, value := range v {\n  1022→\t\t\tif value == nil {\n  1023→\t\t\t\t// Frontend removes null values via JSON serialization, so we should too\n  1024→\t\t\t\t// No special case needed for threshold steps\n  1025→\t\t\t\tdelete(v, key)\n  1026→\t\t\t} else {\n  1027→\t\t\t\t// Recursively process nested values\n  1028→\t\t\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(value, panelType)\n  1029→\t\t\t}\n  1030→\t\t}\n  1031→\tcase []interface{}:\n  1032→\t\t// Process array elements\n  1033→\t\tfor _, item := range v {\n  1034→\t\t\tif item != nil {\n  1035→\t\t\t\tremoveNullValuesRecursivelyWithContext(item, panelType)\n  1036→\t\t\t}\n  1037→\t\t}\n  1038→\t}\n  1039→}\n  1040→\n  1041→// removeIfDefaultValue removes the key from the map if its value equals the defaultValue\n  1042→func removeIfDefaultValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue interface{}) {\n  1043→\tif val, ok := data[key]; ok && isEqual(val, defaultValue) {\n  1044→\t\tdelete(data, key)\n  1045→\t}\n  1046→}\n  1047→\n  1048→// cleanupDashboardDefaults removes dashboard-level default values that frontend filters out\n  1049→func cleanupDashboardDefaults(dashboard map[string]interface{}) {\n  1050→\t// Remove style if it's the default \"dark\" value\n  1051→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"style\", \"dark\")\n  1052→\n  1053→\t// Remove hideControls if it's the default false value\n  1054→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"hideControls\", false)\n  1055→\n  1056→\t// Remove dashboard id if it's null\n  1057→\tremoveIfDefaultValue(dashboard, \"id\", nil)\n  1058→\n  1059→\t// Remove version property - it's managed by Each migration transforms dashboards from one schema version to the next, allowing older dashboards to work with newer Grafana versions.\n    39→\n    40→## Current Schema Versions\n    41→\n    42→- **Minimum Version**: 13\n    43→- **Latest Version**: 42\n    44→- **Backend Location**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`\n    45→- **Frontend Location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n    46→\n    47→## Creating a New Migration\n    48→\n    49→### Step 1: Create the Migration File\n    50→\n    51→Create a new file: `v{N}.go` where `{N}` is the target schema version.\n    52→\n    53→```go\n    54→package schemaversion\n    55→\n    56→import \"context\"\n    57→\n    58→// V{N} migrates [describe what this migration does].\n    59→//\n    60→// [Detailed description of the migration including:]\n    61→// - What properties are being changed\n    62→// - Why the migration is necessary\n    63→// - Any special handling or edge cases\n    64→//\n    65→// Example before migration:\n    66→//\n    67→//\t\"panels\": [\n    68→//\t  {\n    69→//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    70→//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    71→//\t    \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n    72→//\t  }\n    73→//\t]\n    74→//\n    75→// Example after migration:\n    76→//\n    77→//\t\"panels\": [\n    78→//\t  {\n    79→//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    80→//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    81→//\t    \"newProperty\": \"value\"\n    82→//\t  }\n    83→//\t]\n    84→func V{N}(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n    85→\tdashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = {N}\n    86→\n    87→\t// Your migration logic here\n    88→\t// Transform dashboard properties as needed\n    89→\n    90→\treturn nil\n    91→}\n    92→```\n    93→\n    94→### Step 2: Register the Migration\n    95→\n    96→Add your migration to `migrations.go`:\n    97→\n    98→```go\n    99→func GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider DataSourceInfoProvider) map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc {\n   100→\treturn map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{\n   101→\t\t// ... existing migrations\n   102→\t\t{N}: V{N},  // Add your migration here\n   103→\t\t// ... rest of migrations\n   104→\t}\n   105→}\n   106→```\n   107→\n   108→### Step 3: Create Test Data\n   109→\n   110→#### Input Test File\n   111→Create `testdata/input/v{N}.{name}.json` with schema version `{N-1}` with scenarios to cover the specific migration:\n   112→\n   113→```json\n   114→{\n   115→  \"title\": \"V{N} Migration Test Dashboard\",\n   116→  \"schemaVersion\": {N-1},\n   117→  \"panels\": [\n   118→    {\n   119→      \"id\": 1,\n   120→      \"type\": \"graph\",\n   121→      \"title\": \"Test Panel\",\n   122→      \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n   123→    }\n   124→  ]\n   125→}\n   126→```\n   127→\n   128→#### Expected Output\n   129→The test system will generate `testdata/output/latest_version/v{N}.{name}.v42.json` automatically.\n   130→\n   131→### Step 4: Run Tests\n   132→\n   133→```bash\n   134→# Run migration tests\n   135→go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n   136→\n   137→# Run specific migration test\n   138→go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n   139→```\n   140→\n   141→For comprehensive testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   142→\n   143→### Step 5: Frontend-Backend Consistency Validation\n   144→\n   145→Implement different changes in the migration until frontend matches exactly with the backend side. Add as many scenarios as possible to ensure comprehensive coverage of all use cases.\n   146→\n   147→For detailed testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   148→\n   149→#### Test Scenarios to Cover\n   150→\n   151→**Panel-Level Changes:**\n   152→- Panels with different types (graph, table, stat, etc.)\n   153→- Panels with nested panels (rows)\n   154→- Panels with various property combinations\n   155→- Panels with missing or null properties\n   156→- Panels with deprecated properties\n   157→\n   158→**Dashboard-Level Changes:**\n   159→- Dashboard properties (title, tags, time, etc.)\n   160→- Templating variables (query, textbox, custom, etc.)\n   161→- Annotations and links\n   162→- Time picker settings\n   163→- Refresh settings\n   164→\n   165→**Edge Cases:**\n   166→- Empty dashboards\n   167→- Dashboards with only rows\n   168→- Dashboards with mixed panel types\n   169→- Dashboards with complex nested structures\n   170→- Dashboards with invalid or malformed data\n   171→\n   172→**Property Transformations:**\n   173→- Property renaming scenarios\n   174→- Property type conversions\n   175→- Property value transformations\n   176→- Property removal scenarios\n   177→- Property addition scenarios\n   178→\n   179→#### Validation Process\n   180→\n   181→1. **Create comprehensive test data** covering all scenarios\n   182→2. **Run backend migration** and capture output\n   183→3. **Run frontend migration** and capture output\n   184→4. **Compare outputs** using strict equality checks\n   185→5. **Iterate on migration logic** until outputs match exactly\n   186→6. **Add more test cases** for any discrepancies found\n   187→\n   188→#### Test Data Requirements\n   189→\n   190→Create multiple test files for each migration:\n   191→- `v{N}.basic.{name}.json` - Basic functionality\n   192→- `v{N}.edge_cases.{name}.json` - Edge cases and error conditions\n   193→- `v{N}.complex.{name}.json` - Complex dashboard structures\n   194→- `v{N}.property_changes.{name}.json` - Property transformation scenarios\n   195→\n   196→### Step 6: Unit Testing\n   197→\n   198→Add comprehensive unit tests for both backend and frontend migrations to ensure the correct logic is implemented.\n   199→\n   200→#### Backend Unit Tests\n   201→\n   202→Create unit tests in `v{N}_test.go`:\n   203→\n   204→```go\n   205→package schemaversion_test\n   206→\n   207→import (\n   208→\t\"context\"\n   209→\t\"testing\"\n   210→\t\"github.com/stretchr/testify/require\"\n Type Assertions\n   369→```go\n   370→// ❌ Wrong - can panic\n   371→value := panel[\"property\"].(string)\n   372→\n   373→// ✅ Correct - safe type assertion\n   374→if value, ok := panel[\"property\"].(string); ok {\n   375→\t// Use value\n   376→}\n   377→```\n   378→\n   379→### 2. Null Handling\n   380→```go\n   381→// ❌ Wrong - removes intentional nulls\n   382→if value == nil {\n   383→\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   384→}\n   385→\n   386→// ✅ Correct - preserve intentional nulls\n   387→if value == nil && !isIntentionallyNull(panel, \"property\") {\n   388→\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   389→}\n   390→```\n   391→\n   392→### 3. Nested Panel Processing\n   393→```go\n   394→// ❌ Wrong - misses nested panels\n   395→for _, panel := range panels {\n   396→\tmigratePanel(panel)\n   397→}\n   398→\n   399→// ✅ Correct - handles nested panels\n   400→for _, panel := range panels {\n   401→\tmigratePanelRecursively(panel)\n   402→}\n   403→```\n   404→\n   405→## Migration Beyond v42\n   406→\n   407→**Important**: Schema version 42 is the final version for the v1 dashboard API. For new migrations beyond v42:\n   408→\n   409→1. **Backend**: Continue adding schema versions in Go\n   410→2. **Frontend**: Use panel-specific migration handlers instead of schema versions\n   411→3. **Justification Required**: Each new migration must be properly justified\n   412→4. **v2 Transition**: Consider the impact on the transition to schema v2\n   413→\n   414→### When to Add Schema Migrations vs Panel Migrations\n   415→\n   416→**Add Schema Migration** when:\n   417→- Changes affect dashboard-level properties\n   418→- Cross-panel transformations are needed\n   419→- Backward compatibility requires schema version increment\n   420→- **With proper justification** about why it can't be handled as panel migration\n   421→\n   422→**Use Panel-Specific Migrations** when:\n   423→- Changes are panel-type specific\n   424→- Can be handled within individual panel plugins\n   425→- Don't require dashboard-level schema changes\n   426→\n   427→## Testing Guidelines\n [Single Version Migration Testing](#single-version-migration-testing)\n- [Resources](#resources)\n- [Getting Help](#getting-help)\n\n## Overview\n\nDashboard schema migrations ensure backward compatibility as the dashboard data model evolves. Each migration transforms dashboards from one schema version to the next, allowing older dashboards to work with newer Grafana versions.\n\n## Current Schema Versions\n\n- **Minimum Version**: 13\n- **Latest Version**: 42\n- **Backend Location**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`\n- **Frontend Location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n\n## Creating a New Migration\n\n### Step 1: Create the Migration File\n\nCreate a new file: `v{N}.go` where `{N}` is the target schema version.\n\n```go\npackage schemaversion\n\nimport \"context\"\n\n// V{N} migrates [describe what this migration does].\n//\n// [Detailed description of the migration including:]\n// - What properties are being changed\n// - Why the migration is necessary\n// - Any special handling or edge cases\n//\n// Example before migration:\n//\n//\t\"panels\": [\n//\t  {\n//\t    \"id\": 1,\n//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n//\t    \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n//\t  }\n//\t]\n//\n// Example after migration:\n//\n//\t\"panels\": [\n//\t  {\n//\t    \"id\": 1,\n//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n//\t    \"newProperty\": \"value\"\n//\t  }\n//\t]\nfunc V{N}(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n\tdashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = {N}\n\n\t// Your migration logic here\n\t// Transform dashboard properties as needed\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n```\n\n### Step 2: Register the Migration\n\nAdd your migration to `migrations.go`:\n\n```go\nfunc GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider DataSourceInfoProvider) map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc {\n\treturn map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{\n\t\t// ... existing migrations\n\t\t{N}: V{N},  // Add your migration here\n\t\t// ... rest of migrations\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n### Step 3: Create Test Data\n\n#### Input Test File\nCreate `testdata/input/v{N}.{name}.json` with schema version `{N-1}` with scenarios to cover the specific migration:\n\n```json\n{\n  \"title\": \"V{N} Migration Test Dashboard\",\n  \"schemaVersion\": {N-1},\n  \"panels\": [\n    {\n      \"id\": 1,\n      \"type\": \"graph\",\n      \"title\": \"Test Panel\",\n      \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n    }\n  ]\n}\n```\n\n#### Expected Output\nThe test system will generate `testdata/output/latest_version/v{N}.{name}.v42.json` automatically.\n\n### Step 4: Run Tests\n\n```bash\n# Run migration tests\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n\n# Run specific migration test\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n```\n\nFor comprehensive testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n\n### Step 5: Frontend-Backend Consistency Validation\n\nImplement different changes in the migration until frontend matches exactly with the backend side. Add as many scenarios as possible to ensure comprehensive coverage of all use cases.\n\nFor detailed testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n\n#### Test Scenarios to Cover\n\n**Panel-Level Changes:**\n- Panels with different types (graph, table, stat, etc.)\n- Panels with nested panels (rows)\n- Panels with various property combinations\n- Panels with missing or null properties\n- Panels with deprecated properties\n\n**Dashboard-Level Changes:**\n- Dashboard properties (title, tags, time, etc.)\n- Templating variables (query, textbox, custom, etc.)\n- Annotations and links\n- Time picker settings\n- Refresh settings\n\n**Edge Cases:**\n- Empty dashboards\n- Dashboards with only rows\n- Dashboards with mixed panel types\n- Dashboards with complex nested structures\n- Dashboards with invalid or malformed data\n\n**Property Transformations:**\n- Property renaming scenarios\n- Property type conversions\n- Property value transformations\n- Property removal scenarios\n- Property addition scenarios\n\n#### Validation Process\n\n1. **Create comprehensive test data** covering all scenarios\n2. **Run backend migration** and capture output\n3. **Run frontend migration** and capture output\n4. **Compare outputs** using strict equality checks\n5. **Iterate on migration logic** until outputs match exactly\n6. **Add more test cases** for any discrepancies found\n\n#### Test Data Requirements\n\nCreate multiple test files for each migration:\n- `v{N}.basic.{name}.json` - Basic functionality\n- `v{N}.edge_cases.{name}.json` - Edge cases and error conditions\n- `v{N}.complex.{name}.json` - Complex dashboard structures\n- `v{N}.property_changes.{name}.json` - Property transformation scenarios\n\n### Step 6: Unit Testing\n\nAdd comprehensive unit tests for both backend and frontend migrations to ensure the correct logic is implemented.\n\n#### Backend Unit Tests\n\nCreate unit tests in `v{N}_test.go`:\n\n```go\npackage schemaversion_test\n\nimport (\n\t\"context\"\n\t\"testing\"\n\t\"github.com/stretchr/testify/require\"\n\t\"github.com/grafana/grafana/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion\"\n)\n\nfunc TestV{N}(t *testing.T) {\n\ttests := schemaversion.V{N}(context.Background(), tt.input)\n\t\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\t\t\trequire.Equal(t, tt.expected, tt.input)\n\t\t})\n\t}\n}\n```\n\n#### Frontend Unit Tests\n\nCreate unit tests in `DashboardMigrator.test.ts`:\n\n```typescript\ndescribe('V{N} Migration', () => {\n  it('should migrate basic property changes', () => {\n    const dashboard = {\n      schemaVersion: {N-1},\n      panels: [\n        {\n          id: 1,\n          type: 'graph',\n          oldProperty: 'value'\n        }\n      ]\n    };\n\n    const model = new DashboardModel(dashboard);\n dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t// Process panels\n}\n```\n\n## Common Pitfalls\n\n### 1. Type Assertions\n```go\n// ❌ Wrong - can panic\nvalue := panel[\"property\"].(string)\n\n// ✅ Correct - safe type assertion\nif value, ok := panel[\"property\"].(string); ok {\n\t// Use value\n}\n```\n\n### 2. Null Handling\n```go\n// ❌ Wrong - removes intentional nulls\nif value == nil {\n\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n}\n\n// ✅ Correct - preserve intentional nulls\nif value == nil && !isIntentionallyNull(panel, \"property\") {\n\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n}\n```\n\n### 3. Nested Panel Processing\n```go\n// ❌ Wrong - misses nested panels\nfor _, panel := range panels {\n\tmigratePanel(panel)\n}\n\n// ✅ Correct - handles nested panels\nfor _, panel := range panels {\n\tmigratePanelRecursively(panel)\n}\n```\n\n## Migration Beyond v42\n\n**Important**: Schema version 42 is the final version for the v1 dashboard API. For new migrations beyond v42:\n\n1. **Backend**: Continue adding schema versions in Go\n2. **Frontend**: Use panel-specific migration handlers instead of schema versions\n3. **Justification Required**: Each new migration must be properly justified\n4. **v2 Transition**: Consider the impact on the transition to schema v2\n\n### When to Add Schema Migrations vs Panel Migrations\n\n**Add Schema Migration** when:\n- Changes affect dashboard-level properties\n- Cross-panel transformations are needed\n- Backward compatibility requires schema version increment\n- **With proper justification** about why it can't be handled as panel migration\n\n**Use Panel-Specific Migrations** when:\n- Changes are panel-type specific\n- Can be handled within individual panel plugins\n- Don't require dashboard-level schema changes\n\n## Testing Guidelines\n\n### Test File Naming\n- Input: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.json`\n- Output: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.v42.json`\n\n### Test Data all migration tests\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n\n# Run specific test\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n\n# Run with verbose output\ngo test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -v\n```\n\n## Comprehensive Testing Strategy\n\n### Backend Migration Tests\n\nThe backend migration tests validate schema version migrations and API Looking at the frontend migration (lines 644-674), I notice something important:\n\n```typescript\nif (oldVersion < 38 && finalTargetVersion >= 38) {\n  panelUpgrades.push((panel: PanelModel) => {\n    if (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {\n      const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;\n\n      // Update field configuration\n      if (displayMode !== undefined) {\n        // Migrate any options for the panel\n        panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayMode);\n\n        // Delete the legacy field\n        delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.displayMode;\n      }\n\n      // Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\n      if (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n        for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {\n          for (let j = 0; j < (override.properties?.length || 0); j++) {\n            let overrideDisplayMode = override.properties[j].value;\n            if (override.properties[j].id === 'custom.displayMode') {\n              override.properties[j].id = 'custom.cellOptions';\n              override.properties[j].value = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(overrideDisplayMode);\n            }\n          }\n        }\n      }\n    }\n\n    return panel;\n  });\n}\n```\n\nThe frontend code handles overrides REGARDLESS of whether `fieldConfig.defaults.custom.displayMode` exists. The overrides migration happens in the second block (lines 659-669), which is independent of whether the defaults had displayMode.\n\nNow let me compare this with the backend V38 code:\n\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})if !ok {\n    continue  // <-- SKIPS THE ENTIRE PANEL}\n\n\n```\n\nThe backend has a critical flaw: it skips processing the entire panel if `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` doesn't exist, which means overrides never get migrated for panels without explicit defaults. The frontend, however, always processes overrides regardless of whether defaults contain displayMode. This mismatch is the root cause—when a dashboard with table panels lacking explicit defaults gets migrated, the backend leaves the overrides untouched while the frontend expects them to be transformed.\n\nThe sequence is: a table panel with `fieldConfig.overrides` containing `custom.displayMode` but no explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` gets imported. The frontend auto-generates defaults and overrides, but the backend migration skips the panel entirely and never converts the override properties from `custom.displayMode` to `custom.cellOptions`. The code:\n\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n```\n\nThis causes the entire panel to be skipped if `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` doesn't exist. However, this is problematic because:\n\n1. When a dashboard is imported without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`, the frontend defaults create an empty `fieldConfig.defaults = {}`\n2. If the dashboard has field overrides with `custom.displayMode`, those overrides still need to be migrated to `custom.cellOptions`\n3. The `migrateOverrides` function (lines 139-180) is never called for panels without explicit `defaults.custom`\n4. This means field overrides with `custom.displayMode` are never migrated, breaking table formatting\n\n**Why dashboards WITH explicit `defaults.custom` work:**\n- They don't trigger the early `continue` on line 122\n- The entire migration runs, including `migrateOverrides` on line 135\n- Field overrides are properly converted\n\n**The Frontend Behavior (for comparison):**\nThe frontend migration (DashboardMigrator.ts, lines 659-669) ALWAYS processes field overrides regardless of whether there's a displayMode in defaults. This is the correct behavior.\n\n**Missing Test Coverage:**\nThe V38 test file (v38_test.go) doesn't include a test case for a table panel that:\n- Has field overrides with `custom.displayMode`\n- But does NOT have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\nThis missing test is why the bug wasn't caught.\n\n**Affected Components:**\n- `v38.go`: processPanelsV38 function (lines 90-137)\n\n\n- This breaks table column formatting (widths, alignment, display modes) for all dashboards imported without explicit field config defaults.\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**File:** `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`\n**Function:** `processPanelsV38` (lines 90-137)\n**Lines:** 120-123\n\nThe migration contains a premature exit condition that skips the entire panel processing:\n\n```go\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // <-- EXITS PANEL PROCESSING ENTIRELY\n}\n```\n\n### Why This Causes the Regression\n\n1. **Frontend Defaults Creation Flow** (`frontend_defaults.go:102-117`):\n   - When a panel lacks `fieldConfig`, the code creates: `fieldConfig: { defaults: {}, overrides: [] }`\n   - **Critical:** This does NOT create `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` - it remains absent\n\n2. **Migration Execution Order** (`migrate.go:51-127`):\n   - Step 1.1 (line 71): Track original `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` presence\n   - Step 2 (line 75): Apply frontend defaults (creates empty defaults without custom)\n   - Step 5 (line 119): Run schema version migrations including V38\n\n3. **The Bug Trigger**:\n   - For dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`:\n     - `defaults[\"custom\"]` doesn't exist after step 2\n     - V38 hits the `if !ok { continue }` and skips the panel\n     - Field overrides with `custom.displayMode` are never migrated\n     - `migrateOverrides()` (line 135) never executes\n\n4. **Result**:\n   - Field overrides retain `custom.displayMode` instead of being converted to `custom.cellOptions`\n   - Frontend table rendering fails because it expects `custom.cellOptions` (v38+ format)\n   - Column formatting is lost\n\n## Why Dashboards WITH Explicit `defaults.custom` Work\n\nWhen a dashboard **explicitly includes** `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` in its JSON:\n- The type assertion on line 120 succeeds\n- The early `continue` is not triggered\n- Both the defaults migration (lines 126-132) and the overrides migration (line 135) execute\n- Field overrides are properly converted via `migrateOverrides()`\n- Table formatting works correctly\n\n## Frontend Behavior (Correct Implementation)\n\n**File:** `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n**Lines:** 644-674\n\nThe frontend migration demonstrates the correct approach:\n\n```typescript\n// Frontend ALWAYS processes overrides, regardless of defaults.custom\nif (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n  for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {\n    for (let j = 0; j < (override.properties?.length || 0); j++) {\n      if (override.properties[j].id === 'custom.displayMode') {\n        override.properties[j].id = 'custom.cellOptions';  // Always migrated\n      }\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\nThe frontend does NOT use an `if !ok { continue }` approach. It processes overrides unconditionally.\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Problematic Code Pattern\n\n**File:** `v38.go:110-123`\n```go\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // <-- BUG: Skips entire panel if defaults.custom missing\n}\n\n// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n    custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n    delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n}\n\n// This line is never reached if defaults.custom doesn't exist!\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // Line 135\n```\n\n### Missing Test Coverage\n\n**File:** `v38_test.go`\n\nAll test cases (lines 10-443) include explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` definitions. There is **no test case** for the critical scenario:\n- Table panel with field overrides containing `custom.displayMode`\n- BUT WITHOUT explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\nThis is why the regression passed testing.\n\n### Migration Pipeline Timing Issue\n\n**File:** `frontend_defaults.go:102-117`\n\n```go\nif _, exists := panel[\"fieldConfig\"]; !exists {\n    panel[\"fieldConfig\"] = map[string]interface{}{\n        \"defaults\":  map[string]interface{}{},\n        \"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n    }\n} else {\n    if fieldConfig, ok := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n        if _, hasDefaults := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"]; !hasDefaults {\n            fieldConfig[\"defaults\"] = map[string]interface{}{}\n        }\n        // NOTE: defaults.custom is NOT created here\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe frontend defaults ensure `fieldConfig.defaults` exists but explicitly do NOT create `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Packages Involved\n1. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`**\n   - `v38.go` - The problematic migration function\n   - `v38_test.go` - Missing test case for no-defaults.custom scenario\n   - `migrations.go` - Registers V38 migration\n\n2. **`apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/`**\n   - `frontend_defaults.go` - Frontend defaults application logic\n   - `migrate.go` - Migration pipeline orchestration\n\n### Dashboard Schema Version\n- **Affected Range:** v37 → v38 and all subsequent versions (v39-v42)\n- **Regression Introduced:** When V38 was implemented\n- **Triggering Condition:** Any dashboard where:\n  - Panel type is `table`\n  - Original JSON has `fieldConfig.overrides` with `custom.displayMode` properties\n  - Original JSON does NOT have `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` explicitly set\n\n### User-Visible Impact\n- Table columns lose custom display modes (gauges, color backgrounds)\n- Column widths revert to defaults\n- Text alignment settings are lost\n- Dashboards created before v38 with implicit field config are affected\n- Dashboards exported from older Grafana versions without explicit custom defaults\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe V38 migration should be modified to:\n\n1. **Remove the premature exit condition** - Don't skip panels just because `defaults.custom` is missing\n2. **Create defaults.custom if needed** - Ensure the structure exists before processing overrides\n3. **Always process overrides** - Match the frontend behavior of unconditionally migrating override properties\n\n### Code Changes Required\n\nIn `v38.go`, the `processPanelsV38` function should:\n- Process overrides REGARDLESS of whether `defaults.custom` exists\n- Create `defaults.custom` structure if it's needed to store overrides\n- Match the frontend implementation pattern\n\n### Test Coverage\n\nAdd test case to `v38_test.go`:\n- Table panel with `fieldConfig.overrides[].properties[].id = \"custom.displayMode\"`\n- But NO explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n- Verify overrides are properly migrated to `custom.cellOptions`\n\n### Validation\n\nAfter fix, verify:\n1. All field overrides with `custom.displayMode` → `custom.cellOptions` (regardless of defaults.custom presence)\n2. Backward compatibility for dashboards with explicit defaults.custom\n3. Frontend and backend migrations produce identical results\n4. Table panel rendering matches v10.3 behavior\n\n## Files Referenced\n\n| File | Lines | Purpose |\n|------|-------|---------|\n| `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` | 75-137 | Main migration function (buggy) |\n| `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go` | 10-443 | Tests (missing edge case) |\n| `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/frontend_defaults.go` | 102-117, 1150-1169 | Frontend defaults & tracking |\n| `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/migrate.go` | 51-127 | Migration pipeline orchestration |\n| `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts` | 644-674 | Frontend migration (correct) |\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":9,"cache_creation_input_tokens":523,"cache_read_input_tokens":65884,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":523},"output_tokens":3,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"fb8a532c-754a-4d9f-b2d2-6375afd59572","uuid":"5bd92d1a-a41f-4804-9bcf-8dc1114b8652"}
